The Food of the Zhoukoudian Ancient Peking Man (Middle) 121

— Original by Dr. Ralph W. Chaney, Translated by Chen Shaoyan

Because he was discovered near Beijing, he is called "Peking Man." The scientific name is: *Sinanthropus pekinensis*. "Peking Man's" skill can also be proven by the crude quartz fragments that have been found, because these quartz fragments were used as tools for cutting and scraping. "Peking Man" already knew how to use fire, as can be seen from the several feet of ashes, which were deeply piled against the cave wall. Perhaps the "Peking Women" were too lazy to move them out of the cave, so they just casually swept them there.

Several very meaningful discoveries have already been made in these accumulated ash layers. From the incompletely burned firewood, it can be recognized that they are the same as the plants that grow in northern China or other dry and cold areas today. There are also a large number of charred bone fragments, which indicate that horse meat, bison, rhinoceros, and other past animals produced in the Western Hills or nearby plains were cooked here. These animals no longer exist in northern China today.

The fact that these many animals were selected by "Peking Man" as food proves that this area was once a vast open plain, or perhaps there were woodlands alongside surviving streams, just like the semi-arid areas today. The fact that "Peking Man" lived in the cave and had to make fire to keep warm or cook what he ate can explain the low temperature climate at that time. During the same geological period, most of North America and all of Europe were covered by glaciers. Therefore, this era is generally referred to as the Ice Age in the history of the earth. At that time, there were no glaciers in northeastern Asia, because the weather was relatively dry.

More than twenty feet away from the most primitive residence of this ancient human, many various man-made quartz tools and bone fragments were discovered in the breccia. There was also a layer several inches thick, all made up of fragments of the hard shells of many fruit pits. From the texture on the shell surface, it can be determined that it is the shell of the *Celtis* pit, a small spherical entity, even smaller than a pea. So, how did these seeds get moved into this cave and crushed into fragments? This is a major and important question.

The modern *Celtis* tree is a small tree in the forest that grows in North America and Asia. Its greatest characteristic is that it grows on semi-arid foothills and near streams. Wind and running water, the two most common means of transport, would not bring these fruit pits into the cave. Similarly, it is impossible to assume that these *Celtis* trees grew inside the cave, because direct sunlight is an essential condition for the growth of various higher plants.

It seems undoubtable that this large number of *Celtis* pits were brought in from outside the cave, and the hard shells were crushed when they were eaten. Now the question that arises is: Who brought these hard pits into the Zhoukoudian cave? Was it the earliest humans or some other kind of animal?

The *Celtis* fruit has a plain appearance and looks like a small cherry, with a skin and pulp covering a hard pit, which contains the seed. In extremely arid areas of the United States, these fruits are used as food by birds, rodents, and Native Americans. Several kinds of trees and shrubs that bear large and sweet fruits are often harvested by the Native Americans in the Southwest at specific times.

Usually, the fruit is eaten in the same way as cherries. The skin and pulp are swallowed, and the whole pit is either discarded or chewed into fragments, with the larger pieces spit out of the mouth.

The most common use of this fruit is to add flavor to meats and breads. The fruit is crushed, the juice is squeezed out, and then it is cooked with other foods. Finally, the remaining hard shell fragments are discarded. If "Peking Man" ate *Celtis* fruits in the same way as described above, then we hope to find out the truth by studying the accumulated fragments in his cave.

Fossilized bones of rodents were also found in the Zhoukoudian cave. Therefore, it is suspected that it was these rodents, rather than "Peking Man," who brought the *Celtis* fruits into the cave, leaving the pits behind to accumulate. This is a possibility, and much effort has been spent on studying how similar rodents that live today open the hard shells of *Celtis* fruits to obtain the edible seeds inside.

Burnt firewood remains in the ash layer of the cave.

Page 8

Establishment of the Hebei-Chahar Political Council's Construction Committee: Repairing Roads and Building Water Conservancy and Agricultural Projects in the Two Provinces 122

(Beiping Correspondence) The Construction Committee established by the Hebei-Chahar Political Council was formally established yesterday (20th) morning in the former Ministry of Finance. Chairman Men Zhizhong, committee members Wang Jingru, Fu Baoheng, Ji Liang, Zhang Lisheng, Wei Shaowu, Qiao Shiving, Xu Shaojian, and others attended. Song Zheyuan, Chairman of the Political Council, was unable to attend as he was in Tianjin and had not returned, and entrusted Political Council member Liu Zhe to attend and deliver instructions on his behalf. This (21st) morning, the committee held its first meeting and resolved four cases. Subsequent routine meetings will be held once a month on the first of each month. The establishment process, the resolutions of the first meeting, and the committee's organizational rules are recorded separately as follows:

Establishment Process

At 10:00 AM yesterday morning, the committee held its founding ceremony. More than a hundred representatives from military and political agencies attended. First, Liu Zhe delivered instructions on behalf of Song Zheyuan, explaining the mission and significance of the committee's establishment. Then, Chairman Men Zhizhong reported on the establishment process, saying that since Chairman Song appointed him as the Director of Highways on March 1st of this year, he had immediately started repairing roads. Since construction began, more than 2,000 *li* of dirt roads have been completed. However, it was inconvenient to handle affairs with various parties in his personal capacity. After several meetings of the Political Council, it was decided to establish a construction committee to jointly promote progress. Currently, the construction projects in Hebei and Chahar provinces include water conservancy, agriculture, and mining in addition to highways. In the future, they will be gradually implemented within the scope of economic feasibility, and so on.

First Meeting: The first meeting was convened at 10:00 AM this morning. Matters reported: Committee member Wang Jingru reported that the project to dredge the central waterway and build embankments in the Yongding River Delta had been agreed upon with the North China Water Conservancy Commission, and a joint engineering office had been established to take charge. Preparations were complete, and work had begun. A record should be filed. Matters discussed: Men Zhizhong proposed that the detailed rules for the committee's work be submitted to the committee members for review. Wang Jingru proposed that the flooding of the lower reaches of the Jiutuo River in Hebei Province was harmful. Could the committee take overall planning responsibility and submit a request to the National Economic Council to allocate funds to mitigate the water disaster? Resolution: Approved in principle, to be submitted to Ji Liang, Fu Baoheng, and Wei Shaowu for review. Wang Jingru proposed to loan money for sinking wells to alleviate the drought disaster. Resolution: To be submitted for review. Other matters: The meeting adjourned at around 12:00 PM.

Organizational Rules

The committee's organizational rules were announced this morning. The full text is as follows: Article 1: The Construction Committee is organized in accordance with Article 8 of the Provisional Organization Outline of the Hebei-Chahar Political Council. Article 2: The responsibilities of the committee are as follows: Supervision and command of various construction agencies in Hebei, Chahar, Beiping, and Tianjin. Construction and management of various highways in Hebei, Chahar, Beiping, and Tianjin. Promotion and operation of water conservancy projects in Hebei, Chahar, and Tianjin. Reclamation and logging management of forestry in Hebei and Chahar provinces. Improvement and management of coastal fisheries in Hebei Province. Design and mining of mineral products in Hebei and Chahar provinces. Promotion of agriculture and rural cooperation in Hebei and Chahar provinces. Matters referred by the Hebei-Chahar Political Council for discussion. Article 3: The committee shall have seven to nine members, who shall be appointed by the Hebei-Chahar Political Council. The directors of the construction departments of Hebei and Chahar provinces and the directors of the public works bureaus of Beiping and Tianjin shall be ex officio members. Article 4: The committee shall have one chairman, who shall be appointed by the Hebei-Chahar Political Council from among the committee members. Article 5: The committee shall have the following groups: The first group shall be responsible for confidential documents, seals, accounting, general affairs, correspondence, and the formulation of laws and regulations. The second group shall be responsible for the supervision, management, design, investigation, statistics, editing, reporting, and reviewing all proposed construction projects. Article 6: The first group shall have one director, and the group shall be divided into two sections. Each section shall have one chief, six section members, four clerks, and four secretaries to handle all matters under the jurisdiction of each section. The second group shall have one director, six senior technicians, eight technicians and assistant technicians, and four clerks. Article 7: The committee shall have three secretaries, who shall be responsible for general review of correspondence, telegrams, meeting minutes, and other matters. Article 8: The committee may request the Hebei-Chahar Political Council to appoint four to six specialized committee members. Article 9: The committee may establish surveying teams and engineering management offices with the approval of the Hebei-Chahar Political Council when necessary. Article 10: The committee shall hold meetings once a month. Article 11: The committee may convene ad hoc meetings upon the proposal of the chairman or three or more committee members. Article 12: The chairman shall preside over the committee's meetings. If the chairman is absent, the committee members shall elect a temporary chairman. Article 13: The detailed rules for the committee's work, the detailed rules for the conduct of meetings, and the budget shall be determined separately. Article 14: If there are any matters not covered in these rules, they may be amended at any time with the approval of the Hebei-Chahar Political Council. Article 15: These rules shall take effect from the date of their submission, approval, and promulgation.

Sharp Decline in Guangdong Province's Silk Exports: Rayon Fabrics Seize Market Share, Further Restricted by Heavy Foreign Tariffs 123

(Guangzhou Correspondence) The black silk and gauze manufactured in Guangdong Province are excellent products for summer wear and are used both domestically and abroad. In previous years, when sales were brisk, they amounted to no less than several million yuan annually. Domestic sales extended as far as Hubei, Shanghai, and North China, while overseas sales were mainly in Southeast Asia. Tens of thousands of households were engaged in the weaving of silk gauze, with more than 100,000 weavers in Nanhai and Shunde counties. The shops that traded in silk gauze also had strong capital, ranging from tens of thousands to hundreds of thousands of yuan. Since the global economic downturn began, overseas sales have plummeted, while domestic sales have also shrunk due to weak purchasing power. Therefore, most silk gauze shops in Guangzhou have suffered losses in recent years. An investigation into the reasons for the decline in the silk gauze industry in recent years reveals several factors. First, foreign rayon is dumped into the market, and rayon fabrics seize market share. Second, foreign tariffs restrict exports, preventing them from flowing freely as they did in the past. Recently, the Southeast Asian market has been dominated by foreign rayon products, and Guangdong silk gauze has not found a way to restore its former sales volume. In Vietnam, since the establishment of the Sino-French-Vietnamese Commercial Treaty, not only have the previous harsh taxes not been removed, but they have become even more severe. According to a letter recently received by silk gauze shops here from their counterparts in Annam, detailing the situation, which has drawn the attention of those concerned about foreign trade. The letter from Vietnam stated briefly that since the promulgation of the Commercial Treaty, the customs duties levied by the Vietnamese authorities on Chinese silk have not only not been reduced, but have even increased compared to when there was no treaty. Various names are invented to impose arbitrary taxes. Taking Chinese silk as an example, under the old treaty, only the regular tax was levied. Later, when there was no treaty, it was collected at the regular tax rate, with a capital levy added in addition to the regular tax. Now, since the new treaty has been established, the capital levy should be abolished in accordance with the principle of mutual benefit. However, recently, the Vietnamese customs authorities have not only not removed the capital levy, but have also imposed a balancing tax, levied at 25% of the estimated value. For example, the comparison of old and new tax rates for every 100 kilograms of lightweight, dyed, pure silk fabric imported into Annam is as follows: (A) Under the old treaty, the tax rate was 1,360 francs in regular tax. (B) When there was no treaty, the tax rate was 10,000 francs in regular tax and 900 francs in capital levy, totaling 10,900 francs. (C) The recent tax rate after the promulgation of the Commercial Treaty is 8,500 francs in regular tax, 537.5 francs in capital levy, and 2,250 francs in balancing tax, totaling 12,287.5 francs. According to the above examples, it can be seen that after the signing of the new treaty, the import tax rate on Chinese silk in Vietnam is not only higher than under the old treaty, but is also considerably increased compared to when there was no treaty and the ordinary tax rate applied. Although the added balancing tax is said to be levied at 15% of the value, it is estimated according to the exchange rate, which is essentially arbitrary and has no standard. Sometimes, it even reaches 50%. The capital levy, on the other hand, is estimated after compiling all costs and taxes paid, which is essentially taxing taxes. Therefore, the amount of tax paid on imported Chinese silk generally ranges from 100% to 150% of the value. Currently, the Vietnamese market is almost devoid of Chinese silk due to these heavy tax restrictions. Silk gauze merchants hope that the authorities will negotiate with the French and Vietnamese governments to improve the situation, for the sake of business, the national economy, and foreign trade. (April 18th)

Hubei Rural Miscellany 124

(Special Correspondent Cheng Jun) Yangxin's Farms and New Villages

Yangxin suffered a great calamity; its fields were desolate. Recruiting farmers to cultivate the land is indeed a crucial plan. When this reporter arrived in the county seat, I immediately heard that a large-scale collective farm was established fifteen miles from the city. Due to the rain, it was not possible to inspect it earlier, but today's visit was satisfactory. The farm began preparations in August of the 24th year [of the Republic, i.e., 1935]. It repaired the houses that had been burned but not collapsed and established an office to manage affairs. The entire farm has approximately 1,400 mu of land, divided into ten districts, which began cultivation in December of the 24th year. This reporter went to conduct an on-site investigation, traversing each district. The section in Yanglinpu is where the office is located, with three earthen houses enclosed by bamboo fences. A small farmer with a knife guards the entrance. More than twenty disaster-stricken farmers are engaged in digging a pond. Inside the houses are offices, lecture halls, disaster-stricken farmer dormitories, dining halls, cattle pens, etc. Although the area is not large, the arrangement is well-organized. The farm currently has ninety-four disaster-stricken farmers, five female farmers, and four disaster-stricken children, divided into livestock rearing, kitchen staff, and special duty teams. The disaster-stricken farmer teams are divided into six teams, each with ten people, each with a team leader responsible for cultivation. The livestock rearing team has eight people, responsible for herding cattle. The kitchen staff team has five people, responsible for cooking. The special duty team has ten people, responsible for guarding and patrolling, all under military management. The farm grows rice, wheat, beans, hemp, sweet potatoes, etc., varying according to the suitability of the soil. The planned park also plants vegetables, fruits, and trees. When the reporter arrived at the garden, it was the height of peach blossom season, contrasting with the deep green vegetable plots. The lake and mountain scenery felt particularly serene. Beside it, dozens of disaster-stricken farmers were working diligently, building a road. These disaster-stricken farmers mostly come from the Mu Shi Gang and Pai Shi areas. Their parents and brothers were all slaughtered by the Red bandits. They survived the calamity and rely on this place for shelter, avoiding starvation. Their clothing, food, and shelter are all provided by the farm. Each month, they are paid wages of one to two yuan according to their diligence, eight yuan for team leaders, and twelve yuan for foremen. To prevent them from wasting money, a savings department has been established. In terms of education, they have two hours of classes on sunny days and six hours on rainy days, using the Thousand Character Classic as a textbook, primarily focusing on literacy, as well as basic arithmetic, abacus, general knowledge, agricultural common sense, and New Life Movement guidelines. At the same time, military training is emphasized. They conduct morning exercises at dawn and practice martial arts. According to the farm director, the farm has now reclaimed six to seven hundred mu of wasteland, with three to four hundred mu sown. The wasteland reclamation plan has now been changed, and it has been decided to reorganize into a new village, with the disaster-stricken farmers currently cultivating the land as the village masters, allocating land to each household and providing grain according to the number of people. Previously, it was for disaster relief, but now it is for a permanent plan. The current steps for building a new village are divided into three phases to be completed, each phase lasting one year. In the first phase, for the first season, they will still live a collective life, cultivate as much land as possible, and diligently practice military training. Disaster-stricken farmers' families are also allowed to come to the farm to work and be given food and work. After the autumn harvest, twenty excellent individuals will be selected, each given ten mu of land, provided with housing, and lent farming cattle and agricultural tools to help them become self-sufficient and start a family. At the beginning of the second phase, forty disaster-stricken farmers will be recruited. The disaster-stricken farmers who were not allocated land in the previous season will continue to live a collective life, reclaim wasteland, learn to cultivate, be taught etiquette, and be trained in military affairs. After the autumn harvest, forty of the most capable of becoming self-sufficient from the first phase and the best from the second phase will be selected. According to the method of the previous phase, land and housing will be granted, seeds and cattle will be lent, and families will be established. In the third phase, the residents within the transformation area will be tamed to avoid becoming obstacles to the new village. After the autumn harvest, forty households will be separated. In three years, a total of one hundred self-reliant households will be established, meeting the requirements of one bao of a political organization, and the governance will be returned to the bao chief, completing the organization of the new village. The total area of land collectively reclaimed in the three phases is 1,400 mu. Except for the thousand mu divided among the hundred households, the remaining four hundred mu will be collectively cultivated and planted by the villagers of the new village. The income will be used for the support of the elderly and weak in the former collective farm, as well as for the public welfare and education of the village. When the children in the former farm reach adulthood, they will also be allocated land from the four hundred mu according to their names. The important work in progress is, first, the construction of village houses, stipulated to be built purely with thatched wheat and rice straw and rammed earth walls, one house for each household, ten households forming a lian. Next is the purchase of equipment and agricultural tools, which will be given or lent. As for the handling of land rights, the government is requested to issue a notice requiring land owners to register their deeds within a certain period to confirm ownership, giving them a price of one yuan per mu. Those who are willing to join the new village will be allowed to work and enjoy the rights of villagers. Those who are unwilling will be recognized as landlords within three years. If they are unwilling to join and unwilling to rent, a wasteland reclamation fee of ten yuan per mu will be charged. After that, the land will belong entirely to the village. The crops planted in the fields are stipulated to be mainly barley, wheat, and soybeans, supplemented by vegetables. The four hundred mu planted this year will be barley, wheat, broad beans, and peas. In the autumn, sweet potatoes, mung beans, sesame, corn, sorghum, buckwheat, peanuts, and cotton will be the main crops, supplemented by early rice, late rice, dry rice, yams, and tobacco. In addition, because Yanglinpu was formerly used for vegetable gardens, it has been decided to develop a fixed nursery here, dredge wells and ponds, and create new irrigation canals around the garden, planting trees everywhere to arrange roads and support trellises. In front and behind the houses in the new village, attention will be paid to afforestation, mainly with [phase xiang?], all expected to be completed in three years. This kind of farm and new village is the only one of its kind in southern Hubei. It has already achieved preliminary results. Whether it can become a model new village for the entire province depends on the continued efforts of those in charge. (April 2nd)

Anhui Province, Northern Anhui. Shouxian Experiences a Severe Spring Famine with Over 300,000 Disaster Victims. The Provincial Government Plans to Offer Agricultural Loans. 125

Bengbu Correspondence: Shouxian in northern Anhui has always been an impoverished area. The great flood of the 20th year [of the Republic, i.e., 1931] severely damaged the region's vitality. Furthermore, the disturbances by bandits and Reds have caused frequent unrest. The people have already suffered greatly, and their livelihoods are becoming increasingly difficult. In recent years, due to severe drought, the harvest of grains has been poor, and the rural areas have declined to the extreme. This year's spring famine is extremely severe. Most of the food relies on external sources, but neighboring counties mostly restrict exports. Therefore, the food problem has become even more alarming. Areas that previously hoarded grain have often experienced food grabbing incidents. Now, there is nothing left to grab. The total number of disaster victims in the county is estimated to be over 300,000. Elm bark, mulberry bark, cottonseed, and similar items have already been consumed. During the spring, people mostly use green grass, wild vegetables, neem fruit, locust beans, and sweet potato leaves to fill their stomachs. The areas with the most severe disaster conditions include Yaokouji and Yankouji in the first district; Zhuangmuqiao, Dashunji, and Chewangji in the second district; Shuangmiaoji, Yanliumiao, Lisanjiao, and Sanyiji in the third district; Yinxianji, Chongxinji, Yuji, Sanjuesi, and Shiji in the fourth district; and Banqiaoji, Gouqiyuan, and Suwangba in the fifth district. The provincial disaster relief committee has allocated over ten thousand yuan in relief funds, and expatriates from Shouxian have also donated over ten thousand yuan, which has been handed over to local officials and gentry for distribution. However, the disaster area is too vast, and it is a drop in the bucket, unable to provide widespread relief. Recently, with the gap between seasons, people are dying of starvation almost every day. According to local elders, the drought disaster in the sixth year of Xianfeng during the late Qing Dynasty was not as severe as this year. Recently, the Anhui provincial government plans to experiment with offering loans secured by farmland in the county, with an amount of fifty thousand yuan, to be handled by the local bank, as a plan to regulate the rural areas and relieve the disaster-stricken farmers. The local people of Shou eagerly hope for its early implementation to benefit the remaining survivors.

Songjiang: Reckless Bicycles Cause Accidents 127

Yesterday, the young son of Zhao Ayun, a resident of Huayang Bridge, was only four years old. While playing in front of his house, he was tripped by a bicycle ridden by a certain Jia from Jiangbei. The child's hand was caught in the spokes of the wheel, but the rider did not stop, dragging him for five or six feet. A screw on the wheel came loose and pierced the child's arm, about seven or eight tenths of an inch deep. He fainted from the pain, and the Jiangbei man finally stopped. It is reported that after the child was awakened by his family, he had a high fever, and his life is precarious. In the bustling market area around Kuatang Bridge, there have also been many people learning to ride bicycles, recklessly dashing around, causing accidents due to a lack of avoidance. Local people are hoping that the public security authorities will strictly crack down on this to ensure the safety of pedestrians.

Suzhou: Another Rent Riot Erupts in the Countryside of Suzhou 128

Wu County Magistrate Deng Xianghai, in light of the fact that tenant farmers in Guo Xiang, Xiang Cheng, Xie Tang, Yin Shan, and other townships have, on the pretext of last year's poor harvest, refused to pay rent, and that last winter, a rent resistance riot occurred in Yin Shan and other places, causing the county's land rent collection to fall short, with a total collection of only slightly more than 50%, specially formulated a rent payment method, assigning Pan Renxian, Zhang Yijun, and others as rent collection committee members to go to Xie Tang and other townships, assisted by the security team, to urge the collection of land rent. Magistrate Deng also met with Renxian and the rent collection committee members in Guo Xiang on the 21st to summon and instruct the baojia chiefs, urging the farmers to pay rent, and returned to the city that evening. However, the farmers in the Xiatang Village area of the township misunderstood that the county government was using armed force to collect rent. At about 8:00 PM on the 21st, Wu Shengcun and over three hundred other farmers from the township gathered, each carrying torches and reporting to neighboring villages by banging gongs, inciting a riot to resist rent. Captain Shen of the First Squadron of the Security Team stationed in the township immediately led the team to suppress the riot upon seeing the torchlight illuminate the sky. He immediately sent a telegram to the county government to request instructions. The team captured Wang A'jin, the leader of the riot. The farmers became greatly dissatisfied, shouting slogans such as "Down with the Public Security Bureau." Lu En, the eighth district chief of the township, immediately notified the Public Security Bureau to send the water patrol team to rush to the scene overnight to strictly prevent accidents and continued to capture six farmers involved in the incident, including Wang A. Jin. Magistrate Deng reported the situation that night and specially sent the second platoon of the Second Company of the Seventh Battalion of the Security Team and the First Company of Mortars to the township overnight to suppress the riot, ordering them to act appropriately if persuasion was ineffective. The team arrived in the township at 1:00 AM on the 20th and fired a volley of shots into the sky as a demonstration. The farmers gradually dispersed and returned home. Small riots also occurred in Jintang Township, Jin Chen Township, and other places that night, but they were quickly quelled after suppression by the Security Team. Wang A'jin and the other seven people arrested in Guo Xiang Township were escorted to the city on the 22nd. It is reported that Magistrate Deng has decided to severely punish the stubborn farmers who incited the riot and were arrested to warn against lawlessness. As for the three violent farmers, Zhao Huquan and others, arrested in [Only, Wei?] Township, they were also transferred from the Public Security Bureau to the County Government for interrogation on the 12th.

Sealing Up the Xicheng Opium Den 132

The Xicheng opium den outside Guangfu Gate, Hanchang Road, was accused to the Public Security Bureau of adulterating private soil. Director Chen sent police officers from the Supervision Department to search and seize various account books, receipts, and notebooks. The number of opium recorded in the account books was inconsistent, with many discrepancies. The evidence was sent to the county government for review. Subsequently, the county government ordered the Public Security Bureau to subpoena Zhang Yinglin, the manager of the den, and Xue Xiajun, the accountant, for interrogation and bail. Yesterday, the Public Security Bureau, by order of the county government, announced the closure of the den's building, revoked its license, and ceased operations. Inspector Li was sent to execute the order with the police. At that time, the opium smokers in the den were indulging in their habit. Upon seeing the police arrive, they fled in all directions. The den's Suzhou character Fifth Class A license, four account books, ten opium pipes, twenty-one opium lamps, opium paste with a tank weighing nineteen taels, and one hundred and thirteen paper-wrapped opium paste packets, weighing three taels and eight qian, were taken back to the bureau and transferred to the county government for review. At the same time, the building of the den was sealed up immediately.

Clash Between Traffic Police and Postal Workers 134

The traffic police at the railway station had a clash with postal workers yesterday.

Four passengers arrived at the Kai Tong [Open Traffic?] Bus Company and hired a car to go to Meiyuan Xiaojishan for sightseeing. A dispute arose over the car fare. Xia Ruyao, a police officer from the local police section, stepped in to mediate. It is not known how, but the police officer and Zhang Shihong, a driver from the company, had a conflict. At that time, postal worker Yu Wen was on duty outside the bureau and was riding a bicycle to deliver express mail when he was suddenly knocked down in the center of the road. Yu Wen immediately confronted the traffic police, leading to another clash. Police officers Zhu Jinfu and Yang Heng from the section heard of the conflict and came out to mediate, resulting in a direct conflict with Sun Yongchun, You Shiquan, Yu Guisheng, Yu Shousheng, and many other postal workers. As a result, both sides were injured. Five postal workers were taken to the section by the police and then released. They went to the local court to have their injuries examined. After examining the injuries, Prosecutor Shen ordered them to be sent back to resolve the matter themselves. The postal workers' union has decided on three principles for mediation: 1. Medical expenses; 2. Covering wages for workers replacing the injured; 3. Publishing an apology. However, the traffic police section has not accepted the above principles, resulting in a lack of resolution. The postal workers' union convened an emergency meeting of all committee members that day, chaired by Mi Fengyi, to discuss countermeasures. The atmosphere was tense. It was decided to send an official letter to the National Postal Workers' Federation and the general union's Beijing office for support. At the same time, a report was submitted to Du Jiahua, the postal director of the capital, and the Beijing-Shanghai Railway Police Department, appealing for fair treatment. It is reported that postal worker Yu Guisheng suffered injuries to his head and lower abdomen, and Yu Shousheng suffered injuries to his waist and other places. Their injuries are serious, and there may be a danger to their lives.

Changshu: The Rice Mill Workers' Strike Escalates 135

The labor-management dispute at Runfeng Rice Mill, after the labor side's overnight petition, the authorities tried their best to mediate, but due to conditions, the two sides have broken down. Currently, all rice mill workers in the county are on strike, and white rice production has stagnated for three days, and the market situation has been trending higher, affecting the entire society. The Runfeng Rice Mill dismissed four workers, including Zhang Yinchang, and hired non-union members to work, and the union protested, and the dispute lasted for more than eight months without resolution. The night before last, some workers went to the county government to petition, requesting the implementation of the worker's reinstatement, but the section chief of the county government was unable to resolve it, so the workers stayed overnight without dispersing. A telegram was sent to Chief [surname missing] Chen Fu, who was training in Beijing, to return to Changshu for negotiations. Chen returned on the 21st and urgently convened a meeting of labor and management representatives. According to the county magistrate's intention, three points were decided: 1. Runfeng Mill will reimburse Zhang Yinchang 200 yuan, ordering him to resign voluntarily; 2. The hired workers will be introduced to the union by the factory; 3. The machine workers' union will select one more member to be employed by the factory. On the one hand, the machine workers' union will apologize to the factory. However, the labor representatives believed that they were not satisfied, and representatives Zhang Tongyuan, Xu Jianhao, and others left in anger on the spot. The county magistrate believed that the representatives had no sincerity in mediation and suspected that they had incited a strike, so he ordered the representatives to be detained. As a result, the problem became even more serious, and all rice mills in the county went on strike. Subsequently, the Party Department temporarily released those who were detained on bail, but it is expected that the unrest will not subside for the time being.

Yangfu Road Has Started Construction 136

The Suzhou construction plan to extend the Xihu Highway northwards from Yangjian [place name] on that road to Fushan along the river has been surveyed and completed. Roadbed paving has started on the 22nd of this month. This project does not require conscripted labor and has been contracted to a large company in Shanghai. All 2,000 workers have arrived in Changshu. The engineering office is divided into three locations: one from Yangjian to Dahe, one from Dahe to the port, and one from the port to Fushan. The roadbed and bridges are being built simultaneously and are expected to be completed in two months.

City News

Tea Leaf Business of Foreign Firms: Suspension of Draft Acceptance Commences Today; Trade Association Issues a Heartfelt Declaration Explaining the Situation; Yu Qiaqing Cables the Chairman of Anhui Province to Intercede 139

Following the decision by the Foreign Tea Firms Association of Shanghai to suspend draft acceptance from April 21st due to the Anhui Province's control over the transportation and sale of Qimen tea, the Shanghai General Chamber of Commerce persuaded them to postpone the measure by two days. Simultaneously, urgent telegrams were sent to Anhui Province, requesting the swift adoption of the tea industry's suggestions, and a report was submitted to the Shanghai Municipal Government for relaying an urgent appeal to Anhui Province for relief. Yesterday, after receiving a reply from Anhui Province, an emergency general meeting was held at 2 PM, resolving to issue a declaration and implement the suspension of draft acceptance to awaken the authorities. Starting today, all tea firms in the city, including Zhongxin Chang, Hongyuan Yong, Yongxing Long, Zhenhe, Yitai, Yuanfeng Run, Gong Sheng Yong, Shenyuan, Rende Yong, Shengchang Sheng, Yilong, Xietai, Tongtai, Xielong, and others, will suspend draft acceptance and close their businesses. The association's declaration and the exchange of correspondence between Yu Qiaqing and others advocating for the industry are recorded below in their original form:

Association Declaration: A Heartfelt and Urgent Declaration from the Entire Tea Firms of the Shanghai Foreign Tea Firms Association Regarding the Suspension of Draft Acceptance. To Whom It May Concern: Foreign tea leaf business is a major export trade. Since the opening of trade, our industry colleagues have been managing it diligently for over seventy years without interruption. In February of this year, the Agricultural Department of the National Economic Council convened a tea technology discussion conference. The Anhui Provincial Department of Construction suddenly proposed a plan for the transportation and sale of Qihong tea. The result was only a general approval, with the stipulation that the unemployment and debts of export tea merchants, i.e., tea firms, must be taken into consideration. This confirmed that our industry colleagues' business should be maintained. However, to ensure certainty for the future and to avoid unexpected issues, our association again requested the Shanghai General Chamber of Commerce to forward a telegram to the Anhui Provincial Government to inquire about the situation. Subsequently, we received a reply telegram from Anhui, stating that it would not hinder the tea firms from extending loans, and asking us to convey that there was no need for excessive concern. Upon hearing that, the tea firms actively raised funds and advanced loans into the mountains, amounting to over one million yuan. Unexpectedly, on April 1st, the Anhui Provincial Government, together with representatives from the Jiangxi Provincial Government, established the Anhui-Jiangxi Black Tea Transportation and Sales Committee in Anqing, agreeing on a plan to control the transportation and sale of black tea from both provinces, ostensibly to provide relief but in reality aiming for provincial management. After reading the newspaper reports, our association immediately, based on the aforementioned approvals and stating that the tea firms had already lent a large sum of money, thus being closely linked to the tea merchants, and that their own interests were tied to the transportation and sale of tea leaves, so that the debt could be guaranteed, it was imperative that the tea leaves be returned to the firms for sale. If the provincial government, on the one hand, clearly permitted the tea firms to extend loans, and on the other hand, controlled the transportation and sale, it would violate the premise of not hindering tea firms from extending loans and the original intention of building credibility and showing compassion for the merchants' difficulties. Therefore, we submitted a formal request to exempt us from the plan, so as to demonstrate credibility. However, we did not receive a reply. Subsequently, we dispatched representatives, Sun Zifu, Zhuo Jingcheng, and Zhuo Huapu, to Anhui to petition, and personally presented the position of the tea firms, the circumstances of the loans, and all our opinions to the heads of the Finance and Construction Departments. Considering both the government's credibility and the merchants' business, we tentatively drafted a compromise plan, presented the draft clauses with sincerity for negotiation. Secretary Chen of the Construction Department and Section Chief Lu of the Finance Department conveyed that the clauses were fully accepted. If we could obtain the agreement of our colleagues upon returning to Shanghai and submit a formal report, approval would be telegraphed immediately and the government would not extend loans separately, nor would it compete with the people for profit. Subsequently, on the 9th, our association listened to the representatives' report and immediately submitted a formal report by mail. To date, ten days have passed without a reply, yet the provincial government is sending personnel to handle the registration of tea merchants and randomly extending loans. This is a general outline of the development of the industry. In summary, the policies implemented by the provincial government cannot be explained by reason or confirmed by official correspondence. For example, they said that it would not hinder tea firms from extending loans, but now they are extending loans themselves to merchants who have already received loans, which is obviously a hindrance. They said that there was no need for excessive concern, yet the written request was not approved, the representatives were in the province, a plan was drafted and approved in person, and the association's formal report was not approved, which obviously caused people to be very concerned. They said that they were not competing with the people for profit, yet the loan procedures mostly followed the old rules of the tea firms, and the examination of guarantees was even stricter, which was obviously competing for profit. Our colleagues originally had reason to speak of and provincial telegrams to rely on, especially since the tea season has arrived, appeals have been exhausted, and we cannot force the provincial government to show special consideration and give an immediate response. Suspecting the provincial government's intention and the ruthlessness of its methods, all tea firms are in a state of fear. Today they control black tea, tomorrow they will control green tea, and we will all perish together. We have no choice but to consider our lives and property and urgently seek self-preservation measures. We have made clear our situation to the central authorities and decided unanimously to suspend draft acceptance and cease business from April 21st until a proper solution is obtained. Subsequently, the Shanghai General Chamber of Commerce and Mr. Yu Qiaqing strongly urged us to postpone the implementation by two days. At the same time, urgent telegrams were sent to Anhui Province, requesting the adoption of the tea industry's request, and telegrams were sent to the Shanghai Municipal Government to relay the message to Anhui Province. However, as of 5 PM on the 22nd, we had not received a reply from the Anhui Provincial Government. Our association has cried out in vain, without being pitied. Forced by circumstances, we held an emergency meeting and resolved that, starting from April 23rd, under the condition of business suspension, all loan drafts for all export black and green tea in the city, regardless of whether they have been signed or not, will be suspended, to show our determination. We have also sent a letter to the Shanghai General Chamber of Commerce to forward to the banking and finance industries, stating that if this causes disputes, the authorities of Anhui Province must bear full responsibility. Tea firms extend loans mostly by borrowing at interest, stipulating that payment is due upon the sale of tea. Now that there is no tea to sell and the news has spread, who would be willing to lend to tea firms? The bitterness of this situation, where we are facing insurmountable difficulties, is also the result of the Anhui Provincial Government's actions. Alas, the long-standing history of tea firms for decades, and the free business protected by legal guarantees, is like crows wailing in mourning. Is it not fate? The matter is urgent and the change is extraordinary. We have described the whole situation and respectfully request all national industrial and commercial organizations to uphold justice. We will be eternally grateful. This declaration is made with due respect for your consideration.

Ministry of Industry Reply: The Ministry of Industry telegraphed the Municipal Chamber of Commerce: Regarding the Anhui Province's plan to control the transportation and sale of Qimen tea, we have repeatedly consulted the Anhui Provincial Government regarding the telegrams. We will immediately telegraph them to expedite a solution and request them to reply with the control and sales plan for handling. Ministry of Industry, Yang.

Yu Qiaqing Telegram: Yu Qiaqing telegraphed the Chairman of Anhui Province: Urgent, Anqing, Provincial Government, Chairman Liu Junjian. Your telegram is respectfully acknowledged. I immediately persuaded the gentlemen of the Foreign Tea Firms not to suspend draft acceptance or close business, which would cause a huge disturbance. However, all tea firms insisted that the document submitted on the first day was accepted by your government and that it was a final concession. If a decision already approved is reversed, it would not only fail to demonstrate credibility but would also force tea merchants to have no way out. In order to preserve the remaining capital, they are permitted to stop accepting drafts and cease business uniformly on the 23rd. All tea firms have signed. The annual value of foreign black and green boxed tea is 30 million yuan. You love the country and the merchants. I beseech you to follow the will of the people and immediately telegraph your approval of the document submitted on the first day. My ability has been exhausted. Awaiting a reply telegram. Yu Hede bows.

Song's Reply: Zhu Ziwent replied to Yu Qiaqing: Mr. Qiaqing, I have received your letter of April 9th and am fully aware of the situation. The Anhui-Jiangxi Black Tea Transportation and Sales Committee is organized by the governments of Anhui and Jiangxi Provinces. The Economic Committee has no records of it. Having received telegrams from the Shanghai General Chamber of Commerce and the Shanghai Foreign Tea Firms Association, requesting the cancellation of the committee, the committee has telegraphed the governments of Anhui and Jiangxi Provinces to consider the business of the tea firms to alleviate the merchants' difficulties. I am writing to inform you of this matter. Respectfully, Song Ziwent bows.

Jiangsu Bank Adopts District Management System: Jiangsu Province Divided into Eight Districts; Branch Banks Established in Xinpu, Huaiyin, and Bengbu 140

Since Jiangsu Bank switched to a system in the 24th year whereby transactions between branches were routed through the head office, the regulation of capital and management of business have proven very convenient. Currently, there is an urgent need to increase branches, open communication lines, and promote business development. In order to facilitate the planning and implementation of strategies, the supervision of personnel, and the planning and coordination of resources, considering the current transportation situation and commercial trends in Jiangsu Province, all counties in the province are divided into eight districts. One bank in each district is designated as the district management bank, responsible for the planning and guidance of all branches within that district. If it is necessary to establish branches in counties where no branches exist, the district management bank will prepare for and implement the establishment. The division of regions within Jiangsu Province, directly under the head office, consists of eight districts: The Shanghai District, with Shanghai as the district management bank, overseeing Doushan, Chuansha, Nanhui, Fengxian, Songjiang, Jinshan, Jiading, Taicang, Qingpu, Kunshan, Suzhou, Changshu, and Wujiang. The Nanjing District, with Nanjing as the district management bank, overseeing Liuhe, Jiangpu, Jurong, Lishui, and Gaochun. The Zhenjiang District, with Zhenjiang as the district management bank, overseeing Yangzhou, Taiyu, Yizheng, Jiangdu, Gaoyou, Xinghua, Dongtai, Taixian. The Wuxi District, with Wuxi as the district management bank, overseeing Jiangyin, Jingjiang, Changzhou, Yixing, Liyang, Jintan, and Danyang. The Nantong District, with Nantong as the district management bank, overseeing Rugao, Haimen, Qidong, and Chongming. The Xuzhou District, with Xuzhou as the district management bank, overseeing Xiaoxian, Dangshan, Fengxian, Peixian, Pixian, and Suining. The Xinpu District, with Xinpu as the district management bank, overseeing Guanyun, Ganyu, and Shuyang. The Huaiyin District, with Huaiyin as the district management bank, overseeing Huaian, Baoying, Siyang, Lianshui, Suqian, Funing, and Yancheng. As for districts outside the province, there is only the Bengbu eleventh district. According to the new Xinpu, Huaiyin, and Bengbu districts, previously offices, with the implementation of district management, the three locations have been converted into branch banks.

Shunxing Company's Hali Fishing Boat: Sunk by a Japanese Fishing Boat; Eleven Crew Members Rescued by the Japanese Boat; Losses of 20,000 Yuan Will Be Negotiated for Compensation 141

According to the Central News Agency, Shanghai Shunxing Fishing Boat Company owns two fishing boats, Hali and Haiyong, which catch fish in the waters of Jiangsu and Zhejiang. The company received a telegram yesterday from Wu Xinglin, captain of the Hali fishing boat, from Shengshan, stating that at 1:10 AM on April 17, while anchored for rest in the waters northeast of Haijiao, it was suddenly struck by the Japanese fishing boat Jiu Liu Bozhou Maru. The hull was pierced, and within five minutes, the boat sank, with only the mast light visible on the surface. All eleven crew members were rescued by the Japanese fishing boat Jiu Liu Bozhou Maru and sent back to the Haiyong boat. They lost all their clothing and belongings, and the situation was extremely miserable. The loss of the Hali, including the boat price and fishing equipment on board, is estimated to be 20,000 yuan. The company is arranging for the aftermath while awaiting the return of the captain and crew to Shanghai to hear the details of the disaster. Based on the certificate of collision issued by Okato Kanjuro, captain of the Japanese fishing boat Jiu Liu Bozhou Maru, they will negotiate for compensation.

Promotion of National Products in the Northwest: Shanghai National Product Merchants Raise Several Points; Products Can Be Collected Once Agreement Is Reached 145

Ma Hongkui, Chairman of Ningxia Province, came to Shanghai a month ago and contacted local national product manufacturers, requesting them to organize a product exhibition delegation to display their goods in the province during the annual trade fair in order to promote national products in the northwestern border province. Chairman Ma has now returned to the province. The matters concerning the exhibition are being discussed between Zhou Fanwen, owner of the Hezong Trading Company, which manages import and export trade in the province, and the China National Product Promotion Association. According to Wang Weiyao, director of the association, in recent years, authorities in various provinces have paid close attention to and promoted national products. Manufacturers strongly support Chairman Ma's proposal. However, the province is located in the northwest, and transportation is very inconvenient. After large quantities of goods are transported from Shanghai to Xi'an or Baotou, they may be rented cars through Guyuan to reach the destination. The road has only been built the base, and the road surface has not yet been paved. Therefore, there are few merchants traveling back and forth, and adequate protection is required to ensure safety. If camels and horses are hired from Baotou to follow the old commercial roads, it will take a long time, and the transportation costs will be very high. If the products cannot be sold out during the period, they will have to be transported back to Shanghai, which is very uneconomical. Therefore, according to the manufacturers' opinion, if all the products cannot be sold, the provincial government or local merchants must purchase them to avoid losses. The provincial government must provide effective protection for the transportation of goods to ensure safety and exemption from all taxes. Furthermore, the exchange rate between the two places should also be stipulated, as there is no usual exchange relationship between the province and Shanghai, and the provincial government must arrange for exchange from within the government expenses. The above points have been communicated in writing for consultation. If a satisfactory result is achieved, products can be collected in order to rush to the exhibition before the annual trade fair before the old lunar May.

Third Day of the Anti-Smoking Publicity Week: Yesterday Students Gave Speeches; Mayor Wu and Others Broadcast Anti-Smoking and Anti-Drug Messages; Today, More Than Three Thousand Performers Will Promote the Cause; Smokers Can Register Without Paying a Fee 150

The Municipal Party Headquarters of this city has decided to unite with all sectors of society to hold an Anti-Smoking and Anti-Drug Publicity Week. Since its opening on the 20th, the publicity has been very grand and has attracted the attention of citizens. The publicity teams gave speeches along the roads in the past two days, which attracted the attention of citizens. Yesterday (the 22nd) was the third day of Publicity Week and was designated as Student Publicity Day. Today (the 23rd) is the fourth day and is designated as Performers' Publicity Day. More than three thousand performers throughout the city will explain the necessity of anti-smoking and anti-drug measures at any time. Tomorrow (the 24th) is Film Publicity Day, and all cinemas in the city will show anti-smoking and anti-drug films. The details are recorded as follows:

Yesterday, Student Publicity Day

Students Organize Publicity Teams: Yesterday was Student Publicity Day. In addition to famous figures from all walks of life in the city broadcasting speeches on the significance of anti-drug measures, all secondary schools in the city, under the guidance of the Municipal Board of Education, organized publicity teams to set out and conduct publicity in the Nanshi area. It is estimated that more than ten schools, including the Minli Boys' and Girls' School, Junyi School, and Wuben School, sent out publicity teams on this day. Minli Middle School, led by the training officer Deng Zhiping, led 30 students to conduct publicity along Zhaojia Road in the city and posted publicity slogans. China Girls' Middle School, led by the training director Luo Shuzhang, led 25 students, divided into groups, to conduct publicity in Xiaodongmen, Nanmatou, Jiumudi, Ximen, and Xieqiao. Junyi Middle School, led by the training director He Ziguo, led 15 students to conduct publicity in the Xieqiao area. Jingye Middle School, led by Principal Tao Guangchuan and teachers Zhang Siyi and Xu Zhuxu, led 30 students, divided into groups, to conduct publicity in the Yimiao Zhaojia Road and Xiaodongmen areas. Wuben Girls' Middle School, led by teachers Hu Ruisheng and Chen Rongming, led 40 students to conduct publicity along Ximen Zhonghua Road. Each school provided its own white cloth banners and went to various districts to give speeches on the harm of drugs. The audience was quite moved. Shanghai Girls' Middle School is scheduled to depart this afternoon, led by Principal Wu Zhiqian, along with all teachers and students, to parade in the Nanshi area. Teachers Hu Kewen and Fu Xiaofeng, etc., will lead more than 100 girl scouts from the school, divided into groups, to conduct publicity on various roads. Although it was drizzling yesterday, the students were still full of energy, and their spirit of service was commendable.

Famous People Broadcast Anti-Smoking Messages: Yesterday was Student Publicity Day. In addition to the Municipal Bureau of Education mobilizing schools to organize student publicity teams, the preparatory committee also hired Mayor Wu, Commander Yang, Cai Jingjun, Li Ting'an, Wang Xiaolai, Du Yuesheng, Yan Fuqing, Liu Zhanen, Zhang Shoukuang, Li Zhaohuan, Pei Fuheng, and Yu Zuoting, etc., to go to the Municipal Radio Station, Da Zhonghua, Zhongxi, Dongfang, Hangyin, Guohua, Dalu, Mingyuan, Fuyin, Jiaobu, Foyin, and Li Shudetang, etc., to broadcast on wireless radio stations and speak about the dangers of smoking and drugs, and the necessity of banning and resisting them. However, the speeches of each person were too long, so they are omitted.

Today is Performers' Publicity Day

Three Thousand Performers Promote the Cause: Today, according to the Publicity Week schedule, is designated as Performers' Publicity Day. Of the tens of thousands of performers in this city, about three thousand will be mobilized today. The preparatory committee will provide publicity materials, and according to the original performance settings of each performer, they will insert publicity speeches at any time. Such as performance venues, theater broadcast platforms, singing and dancing troupes, and various Tanghui gatherings, are all publicity areas for these people.

Actively Preparing the Lantern Parade: The preparatory committee believes that many people will participate in the lantern parade, and the general public also pays great attention to it. It is indeed the best publicity method. Therefore, in addition to the participating institutions and groups providing their own lamps, a large number of five-color lanterns with pictures and slogans are being made, which are very eye-catching. Other items such as flags are currently being rushed to manufacture.

Tomorrow is Film Publicity Day

Cinemas Add Films: Tomorrow is the fifth day of Publicity Week and belongs to Film Publicity Day. The preparatory committee has specially pre-made a large number of anti-smoking and anti-drug slides and distributed them to major cinemas in the city, such as Jincheng, Mingxing, Zhongyang, Kade, Guanghua, and Gonghe. After the opening advertisement news of each showing and before the feature film is shown, these slides will be added to make the audience aware of the terrible nature of smoking. It is now heard that the authorities of each cinema feel that it is necessary to vigorously promote the prohibition of smoking and drugs, so this film has been added to the screenings since the beginning of Publicity Week.

Command and Discipline Talk: The preparatory committee believes that many people will participate in the lantern parade. In order to cooperate in the division of labor, it is specifically stipulated that each participating institution and group should first elect one chief and one deputy commander, and one chief and one deputy disciplinarian. A discussion meeting was specially convened at 2:00 p.m. yesterday to discuss the various procedures for command and discipline. More than ten chief and deputy commanders and chief and deputy disciplinarians from the Municipal Party Headquarters, the Municipal Chamber of Commerce, the Public Security Bureau, the Municipal Farmers' Association, and the Boy Scout Council, etc., discussed matters related to command and discipline during the lantern parade.

Du Discusses Punishment and Reformation: The Shanghai Municipal Party Headquarters held a broadcast publicity campaign to ban smoking and drugs. Yesterday afternoon, Mr. Du Yuesheng was specially invited to give a speech on "The Punishment and Reformation of Smoking Prohibition" at the Guohua Radio Station. The time was from 3:15 to 4:00 p.m. Mr. Du has always studied the smoking ban policy, so his speech was very thorough. The reporter of the Shen Shi News Agency found and recorded his speech as follows: People from all walks of life, ladies and gentlemen, today, I am honored to be invited by the members of the Municipal Party Headquarters to say a few words for the broadcast promotion of banning marriage and rejecting drugs, so that I can have the opportunity to talk with people from all walks of life. I feel very honored. However, I have little research on this issue and I am not good at words, so I dare not say it is a speech, but just talk to you about my personal feelings. Speaking of the issue of smoking prohibition, there is a long history in our country. The predecessors have made many theories and methods for this problem. In the middle of November last year, I was also invited by the Municipal Bureau of Education to speak at the Zhongxi Radio Station. Once gave a brief report on the situation of the Shanghai Smoking Prohibition Committee. What I want to talk to you today is about the punishment and reformation of smoking prohibition. It is really just a commonplace. Our country's society has always been maintained on morality, and the people's concept of the legal system is very weak. Therefore, it seems not easy to achieve full effect by starting from the strictness of punishment in smoking prohibition. It must be assisted by reformation to complete this work, which is also the purpose of this Publicity Smoking Prohibition. The power of reformation is active and universal, but without the high-hanging punishment in front, the power of reformation may have a day of exhaustion, and there is no way to save it. The government certainly does not want the people to break the law and be punished. It is best to get a rational self-awareness, or be awakened by reformation and automatically eliminate this bad habit. However, the people's attention to the concept of the legal system is an indispensable condition in the voice of smoking prohibition. Now I will talk about the temporary regulations on punishing smoking and the regulations on strictly enforcing smoking cessation and eliminating smokers, and select the important ones. In addition, there are various regulations and regulations. If you propose to talk about it, you can't finish it in a short time. In the future, the Municipal Smoking Prohibition Committee plans to summarize various laws and regulations on smoking prohibition and print them into a separate booklet for people from all walks of life to study. Article 3 of the Provisional Regulations on Punishing Smoking states that those who intend to manufacture opium and plant poppy shall be sentenced to death, life imprisonment, or imprisonment for more than ten years. Article 4 states that those who gather crowds to resist the eradication of tobacco seedlings shall be punished as follows: The principal or on-site commander shall be sentenced to death or life imprisonment; the rest of the crowd shall be sentenced to imprisonment for more than three years but less than ten years. Those who privately sell and transport opium shall be sentenced to life imprisonment or imprisonment for more than three years (and may be fined up to 3,000 yuan). If the quantity is more than 500 taels, they shall be sentenced to death. Those who sell and transport poppy seeds shall be sentenced to imprisonment for more than one year but less than seven years and may be fined up to 1,000 yuan. Those who import from foreign countries shall be sentenced to death, life imprisonment, or imprisonment for more than ten years and may be fined up to 5,000 yuan. The same applies to those who export to foreign countries. Those who open houses for people to smoke opium shall be sentenced to life imprisonment or imprisonment for more than five years and may be fined up to 3,000 yuan. Those who use smoking cessation permits to provide people with smoking for profit shall be sentenced to imprisonment for more than three years but less than seven years and may be fined up to 1,000 yuan. Those who smoke opium shall be sentenced to imprisonment for more than six months but less than two years and may be fined up to 300 yuan. Those who are addicted shall also be ordered to see a doctor within a time limit and be ordered to quit. Those who smoke again after quitting shall be sentenced to imprisonment for more than one year but less than three years and may be fined up to 500 yuan and ordered to quit. Those who commit three offenses shall be sentenced to death. All school teachers and students who commit the above three crimes of opening houses, using permits to provide people with smoking for profit, or smoking opium shall be punished with the heaviest sentence in the original articles. Article of the Provisional Regulations on Drug Prohibition states that the drugs referred to in this regulation refer to morphine, cocaine, and other compounds or various colored pills, caffeine, milk powder, quinacrine, etc., which are compounded or found to be used for manufacturing drugs, shall be treated as drugs. Article 3 stipulates that those who manufacture or transport drugs shall be sentenced to death. Article 4 stipulates that those who sell or possess drugs with the intention of selling them shall be sentenced to death. Article 5 stipulates that those who intend to make a profit by administering morphine to others, or use a house for people to use drugs, shall be sentenced to death. Article 6 stipulates that those who administer morphine or use drugs within the year of the Republic of China shall be sentenced to imprisonment for more than one year but less than three years, and shall be ordered to see a doctor within a time limit and be ordered to quit. Those who re-offend after quitting shall be sentenced to imprisonment for more than three years but less than seven years, and shall be ordered to quit within a time limit, and those who re-offend after re-quitting shall be sentenced to death. Article 7 stipulates that those who commit the crimes in the previous article within the year of the Republic of China shall be sentenced to imprisonment for more than three years but less than seven years, and shall be ordered to see a doctor within a time limit and be ordered to quit. Those who re-offend shall be sentenced to imprisonment for more than seven years and shall be ordered to quit. Those who re-offend after re-quitting shall be sentenced to death. Article 8 stipulates that those who commit the crimes in Articles 3 to 7 of this regulation from the 26th year of the Republic of China shall be sentenced to death. This kind of severe punishment, smoking compatriots, can really realize and wake up. Fortunately, during the period of self-renewal registration, go to register as soon as possible, and start to quit, not only for your own recovery, but also to increase efficiency for the country's revitalization of the nation. Today, leader Chiang Chairman is doing his best to rescue compatriots who have fallen into the sea of ​​suffering. I hope that smoking compatriots will not abandon themselves to the country and not be reformed. This is what I pray for very much.
