Page 15

Popular Lectures

Lin Xiangru and Lian Po 230

— Zheng Kan Tzu

Lin Xiangru and Lian Po were both from the state of Zhao during the late Warring States period. One came from a poor and humble background, while the other was a prominent and powerful figure. They lived during the Warring States period, when seven powerful states (Qin, Chu, Qi, Zhao, Han, Wei, and Yan) coexisted. At that time, each state needed talented individuals to expand its territory or defend against enemies. Therefore, whoever was capable could seize opportunities to become a high-ranking official.

After the death of King Wuling of Zhao (295 BC), although Zhao still possessed some residual power and influence, the "vertical alliance" had disintegrated, and the strength of Qin had accumulated. Zhao could not avoid being coerced by Qin. The people of Zhao were divided: the weak sought to appease Qin for temporary peace, while the strong considered it a disgrace to appease Qin and strived to find ways to save the country. Lin Xiangru and Lian Po were among the strong in Zhao, but due to their different circumstances, their methods of saving the country also differed.

Lian Po was a skilled general in Zhao, capable of winning battles and capturing territory. Naturally, he had opportunities to save the country. Lin Xiangru, on the other hand, came from a poor family and was raised in the household of the eunuch Miao Xian from a young age. Miao Xian was favored by King Huiwen of Zhao (King Wuling's son). He was wealthy and powerful, and like other prominent officials of the time, he supported many retainers. However, he was busy serving King Huiwen and could not discern who was good and who was bad. As Lin Xiangru grew older, he felt ashamed to be a retainer of a eunuch. However, the society at the time was corrupt, making it difficult to find a way out. Moreover, he was eager to serve his country and felt compelled to humble himself to achieve his goals. He often comforted himself, saying, "Personal reputation is a small matter, saving the country and the people is a great matter. If I can emulate Shang Yang and strengthen Zhao as he strengthened Qin, even if I die after achieving success, even if later generations despise my humble origins as a retainer of a eunuch, I would be content." But how could he impress Miao Xian and get him to introduce him to King Huiwen? This was a difficult problem to solve.

One day, an opportunity for him to be appreciated by Miao Xian arrived. Miao Xian unintentionally offended King Huiwen and, fearing punishment, hurriedly packed his belongings to flee to the state of Yan. When his retainers heard this news, they feared being implicated and fled. When Miao Xian sent someone to ask them for advice, only Lin Xiangru came forward. Miao Xian felt that he still had courage and told him his plan to flee to Yan. After listening to Miao Xian, Xiangru stopped him and said, "How do you know that the King of Yan will definitely take you in? If he rejects you or does not treat you with respect, you will have no way out and regret it too late!" Miao Xian replied, "I know that the King of Yan will treat me well. I once accompanied the King (referring to the King of Zhao) to meet the King of Yan on the border. The King of Yan secretly held my hand and said he wanted to befriend me. Therefore, I know the King of Yan likes me, so I want to go and rely on him today." Xiangru shook his head and said, "You are mistaken. Because Zhao is strong and Yan is weak, and you are favored by the King of Zhao, the King of Yan wanted to befriend you. Now that you have offended the King of Zhao and are fleeing to Yan, Yan, fearing Zhao, will certainly not take you in. They will detain you and send you back, which would be a dead end! You should rather bare your arms, carry the instruments of punishment on your back, and plead guilty to the King of Zhao. The King of Zhao is kind and gentle and will surely have mercy on you and pardon your crime." Miao Xian listened to Xiangru's words and was indeed pardoned. From then on, he recognized Xiangru as a man of vision and held him in high regard.

In the fourteenth year of King Huiwen of Zhao, the state of Qin intended to destroy the state of Han and annex the Eastern Zhou. Knowing that the states hated Qi, Qin used Qi as bait to lure Zhao, Han, Wei, and Yan to attack Qi. Qin calculated that after defeating Qi, the states would be exhausted and unable to resist Qin. At that time, Qin could do as it pleased. King Huiwen, unaware of the plot, constantly sent troops to attack Qi. After two years of fighting, it was Lian Po's turn to be the general. He was very brave and skilled in battle and indeed defeated Qi and captured the city of Jinyang. King Huiwen was very pleased and appointed Lian Po as High Minister.

After prolonged warfare, the state of Zhao needed to rest and recuperate. The state of Qin, with malicious intentions, took the opportunity to create trouble for Zhao. At that time, King Huiwen obtained the He Shi Bi jade from the state of Chu, which King Zhaoxiang of Qin learned of and wanted to obtain through deception. He sent a letter to the King of Zhao, saying he was willing to exchange fifteen cities for the jade. After receiving the letter, the King of Zhao immediately discussed it with General Lian Po and other ministers. They feared that if they gave the jade to Qin, they would not receive the fifteen cities and would be deceived by Qin. If they refused to give it, they feared that Qin would send troops to forcibly demand it. They did not know what to do. Therefore, they decided to find an envoy with both wisdom and courage to reply to Qin. Unable to find a suitable person at the time, the King of Zhao summoned Lin Xiangru upon Miao Xian's recommendation. The King of Zhao asked Xiangru, "The King of Qin wants to exchange fifteen cities for my jade. Can I give it to him?" Xiangru replied, "Qin is strong and Zhao is weak. We cannot refuse." The King asked again, "What if he takes my jade and does not give me the cities?" Xiangru explained, "If Qin asks to exchange cities for the jade and Zhao refuses, Zhao is in the wrong. If Zhao gives the jade and Qin does not give Zhao the cities, Qin is in the wrong. Comparing the two, it is better to agree to Qin and let them bear the blame for deceit." The King of Zhao agreed with Xiangru and asked him who could be sent to Qin. Xiangru replied, "Your Majesty cannot find a suitable person. I am willing to take the jade. I will only leave the jade with Qin if Zhao obtains the cities. Otherwise, I will definitely bring the entire jade back intact." At that time, many people who looked down on Lin Xiangru said he was boasting and urged the King of Zhao not to listen to him. The King of Zhao overcame the opposition and finally sent Xiangru as an envoy.

Xiangru bid farewell to the King of Zhao, hid the jade, and took several reliable warriors, heading west to Qin. On the way, Xiangru thought of ways to deal with the King of Qin, looking very serious. His followers thought he was afraid of entering the powerful state of Qin, fearing misfortune, and secretly laughed at his cowardice. In fact, he had already disregarded his own life and death. At that time, his only concern was "how to avoid humiliating the country."

They arrived in Qin. The King of Qin thought his deceptive scheme had succeeded. Seeing that the envoy who brought the jade was a bookish scholar, he became even less wary. When Xiangru arrived, he was sitting in the Zhangtai Palace, entertaining himself with a group of beautiful women. He received Xiangru there. Xiangru personally held the jade and presented it to the King of Qin. The King of Qin, upon seeing the crystal-clear jade and its emerald-green luster, was very pleased. He immediately passed it to his beautiful women and attendants for appraisal. Everyone admired it and cheered "Long live the King!" Xiangru stood there like an extra person, and no one paid attention to him. Xiangru realized that the King of Qin had no intention of exchanging the cities for the jade. He then walked up to the King of Qin and said, "The jade has a flaw. Please allow me to point it out to Your Majesty." The King of Qin immediately gave him the jade. Xiangru took the jade, held it firmly, and retreated a dozen steps, leaning against a pillar. His face turned terrible, his forehead was covered with veins, his hair stood on end, and his hat was about to fall off. In his great anger, he pressed his head against the pillar, straightened his back, and loudly rebuked the King of Qin, saying:

"Your Majesty wanted to obtain this jade and sent a letter to the King of Zhao. Upon receiving your message, the King of Zhao immediately summoned all his ministers for discussion. Everyone said, 'Qin is greedy and relies on its military strength, using the excuse to deceive us for our jade. The promised fifteen cities will probably not be obtained.' Therefore, they considered not giving the jade to Qin. Only I disagreed, saying, 'Even between commoners, there can be deception, let alone between great states? Moreover, offending a great state for such a small matter as a piece of jade is not advisable.' The King of Zhao then listened to my words, fasted for five days, and solemnly handed the jade and a reply letter to me in the court. Why did he do that? Because he respected the great state and showed particular respect. Today, when I arrived, Your Majesty casually received me in the Zhangtai Palace, with very arrogant etiquette. After obtaining the jade, you passed it to the beautiful women to mock me. I saw that Your Majesty had no intention of giving the cities in exchange for the jade. Therefore, I took back the jade. If Your Majesty insists on forcing me, my head and the jade will immediately be smashed on this pillar for Your Majesty to see!" After Xiangru finished speaking, he held the jade in both hands, looking askance at the pillar, posing as if he were about to smash it.

The King of Qin feared that Xiangru would really break the jade. He hurriedly got up to apologize and earnestly asked him not to do so. At this time, the timid beautiful women, frightened and flustered, fled back to the inner palace before the King of Qin could even give the order. The King of Qin then ordered the officials in charge of maps to bring in the map of Qin and point out the fifteen cities from here to there that would be given to Zhao. Xiangru guessed that the King of Qin was deceiving him and would not be fooled. However, to fulfill his promise to the King of Zhao to "return the jade intact" and to uphold his principle of "not humiliating the country," he had to feign compliance with the King of Qin. He said to the King of Qin, "The He Shi Bi jade is a treasure known to the world. The King of Zhao, fearing Your Majesty, dared not refuse to offer it to Your Majesty. The King of Zhao fasted for five days when he sent the jade. Now Your Majesty should also fast for five days and set up the nine-guest ceremony in the court to receive the jade with respect. Only then will I dare to offer the jade." The King of Qin knew that he could not forcibly snatch the jade from Xiangru's hands and had to agree. He asked Xiangru to stay in the Guangcheng Inn to wait.

Xiangru returned to the guesthouse and regained his freedom. He guessed that even though the King of Qin had agreed to fast, he would definitely break his promise and not give Zhao the cities in the future. Therefore, he sent one of the warriors who had come with him, dressed in coarse cloth, disguised as a small merchant, to hide the jade and escape back to Zhao via a side road.

The King of Qin fasted for five days and set up the nine-guest ceremony in the court to receive the envoy of Zhao, Lin Xiangru. Xiangru, upon seeing the King of Qin, was not afraid at all. He first thanked the King of Qin for the grand ceremony and then frankly said to the King of Qin, "Since the time of Duke Mu of Qin, there have been more than twenty rulers who have never truly fulfilled international promises. I fear being deceived by Your Majesty and betraying the state of Zhao. Therefore, I sent someone to send the jade back to Zhao first. You see, Qin is strong and Zhao is weak. If Your Majesty sends an envoy to ask for the jade, Zhao will immediately offer the jade, not afraid of being deceived by a great state. Now that Qin is so strong, if you first cede fifteen cities to Zhao, how dare Zhao keep the jade and offend Your Majesty? I know that deceiving Your Majesty is a crime punishable by death. I have come here to ask for death, hoping that Your Majesty and your ministers will deliberate carefully." The King of Qin and his ministers, unexpectedly hearing these words, looked at each other, both surprised and angry. Everyone gnashed their teeth in hatred. Xiangru remained calm, looking back to see that the warriors who had laughed at his cowardice had been frightened to the point of being pale.

After a while, the King of Qin's anger subsided. His attendants wanted to execute Xiangru, but the King of Qin said to them, "Now that we have killed Xiangru, we still cannot obtain the jade, and we will sever the relationship between Qin and Zhao. It is better to treat him well and send him back to Zhao. Would the King of Zhao deceive Qin for the sake of a piece of jade?" As a result, he received Xiangru with courtesy and sent him back to his country. Xiangru returned to the state of Zhao, and the King of Zhao, because he had served as an envoy without dishonoring the country, considered him virtuous and appointed him as a high minister. Later, the state of Qin did not give the cities to the state of Zhao, and the state of Zhao did not give the jade to the state of Qin.

After a few years, the King of Qin sent someone to tell the King of Zhao that he wanted to meet with the King of Zhao at Mianchi, outside the western He River, to strengthen their relationship. The King of Zhao feared Qin and did not want to go. Xiangru and Lian Po thought that the King's refusal to go would show weakness and greatly humiliate the country. They urged the King of Zhao to go. The King of Zhao had no choice but to go with Xiangru. Lian Po personally escorted them to the border and bid farewell to the King, saying, "Your Majesty, I have calculated that, including the time for travel and gathering, you should return to the country within thirty days. If you do not return after thirty days, I will request that the crown prince be made king to disappoint Qin." The King of Zhao knew that this was the best way to protect the country and consolidate his power, and of course, he agreed.

The King of Qin's invitation to the King of Zhao was actually made with malicious intentions. He originally wanted to wait for the King of Zhao to say "no" so that he could use it as an excuse to send troops to attack the state of Zhao. Unexpectedly, the King of Zhao dared to attend the meeting, which made it difficult for him. He decided to change his approach and use the occasion to humiliate the King of Zhao, making him lose face when he returned to the country. But the prime minister of the King of Zhao was Lin Xiangru, who handled everything according to etiquette, without revealing any flaws. However, the King of Qin was determined to find an opportunity to humiliate the King of Zhao. When the King of Qin was drinking and becoming slightly drunk, he pretended to be very amiable and said to the King of Zhao, "I have heard that the King of Zhao is very good at music. Please grant us a zither performance!" His attendants seized the opportunity to present the zither to the King of Zhao. The King of Zhao, unaware that the King of Qin was intentionally making fun of him, thought that playing along with the occasion would not matter and readily accepted the zither and began to play. After the King of Zhao finished playing the zither, the Qin historian stepped forward and wrote, "On such and such a day, the King of Qin and the King of Zhao met and drank, and the King of Qin ordered the King of Zhao to play the zither." Xiangru knew that the King of Zhao had fallen into a trap. He quickly stepped forward and said, "The King of Zhao has heard that the King of Qin is skilled in Qin music. Please take out a basin and jug and let the King of Qin and the King of Zhao entertain each other." The King of Qin was angry and refused to agree. So Xiangru himself took the jug, knelt, and presented it to the King of Qin. The King of Qin refused to strike the jug. Xiangru frowned and loudly said to the King of Qin, "If Your Majesty is not willing to strike the jug, it shows that Your Majesty intends to humiliate the state of Zhao. In that case, Xiangru will splatter the blood from my neck on Your Majesty within these five steps!" The King of Qin's attendants wanted to kill Xiangru, but Xiangru glared at them and rebuked them, and they all retreated in fear. The King of Qin was very upset and had no choice but to strike the jug reluctantly. Xiangru turned around and ordered the Zhao historian to write, "On such and such a day, the King of Qin struck the jug for the King of Zhao." The Qin ministers asked the King of Zhao to offer fifteen cities to the King of Qin as a birthday gift. Xiangru also asked the King of Qin to offer the capital of Qin, Xianyang, to the King of Zhao as a birthday gift. Tit for tat, Zhao never showed weakness. The King of Qin also saw that the King of Zhao had a strong military presence and knew that the state of Zhao had been prepared for a long time. He dared not act rashly and had to acknowledge his bad luck, allowing the King of Zhao to return to his country safely.

The King of Zhao returned to the state of Zhao, and because Xiangru had made great contributions, he appointed him as a high minister, with a higher position than Lian Po. Lian Po was unconvinced and said, "As a general of Zhao, I have made great contributions in attacking cities and fighting in the field. Lin Xiangru only relied on his eloquence. Now his position is actually higher than mine. There is no such reason! Moreover, Xiangru was originally a lowly person. I am actually below him. How can I not be ashamed?" He also declared, "If I see Xiangru, I will definitely humiliate him."

When Xiangru heard what Lian Po said, he refused to meet him. Every time it was his turn to attend court, Xiangru would always claim illness, not wanting to compete with Lian Po for position. When Xiangru went out, if he saw Lian Po in the distance, he would immediately change his route to avoid him. Xiangru's followers felt that Xiangru's fear of Lian Po was a great shame and urged Xiangru, saying, "The reason we left our relatives to serve you is only because we admire your high moral character. Now that you and Lian Po are colleagues, and Lian Po speaks ill of you, you actually avoid him, fearing him to such an extent. Even ordinary people would feel ashamed of this, let alone generals and ministers? We are unwilling to endure this and have come to bid you farewell." Xiangru asked them, "Who do you think is more formidable, General Lian or the King of Qin?" They answered in unison, "General Lian is no match." Xiangru then further said to them, "You see, with the King of Qin's power, Xiangru dared to rebuke him in court and humiliate his ministers. Although Xiangru is useless, how can I be afraid of General Lian alone? However, I think that the reason why the powerful Qin dares not send troops against Zhao is only because there are the two of us. If the two tigers fight, they will inevitably not both survive. No matter which of us is injured or killed, Qin troops will come to the border of Zhao sooner or later. The reason why I would rather suffer losses myself and not fight with General Lian is to prioritize the country's crisis over personal feuds." Xiangru's followers then realized the truth and marveled at Xiangru's greatness.

Xiangru's words quickly spread to Lian Po. Lian Po, upon hearing them, was ashamed and constantly reproached himself, saying, "I am a true villain! I am a true villain!" So he asked a guest to mediate with Xiangru, bared his upper body, carried thorns on his back, and personally went to Xiangru's residence to apologize, saying, "I, a lowly person, did not know that you, sir, were so generous!" Xiangru, hearing Lian Po's remorseful words, could not help but be moved to tears. Later, the two became very good friends, and the state of Zhao prospered because of their cooperation, and no one dared to bully it again.

Publishing World

A Special Publication for the "Poverty is Not a Crime" Performance

At the invitation of the Shanghai Theatre, this association has compiled the position of the current "Publishing World" into a special publication for the "Poverty is Not a Crime" performance, to be presented to the audience of "Poverty is Not a Crime." We respectfully request that readers pay attention to it!

Respectfully presented by the Publishing Affairs Committee of the China Cultural Construction Association.

Revision of the Script for "Poverty is Not a Crime" 231

— Xiang Peiliang

The Shanghai Theatre's decision to perform "Poverty is Not a Crime" is based on Zheng Zhenduo's translation and has been revised. There are three types of revisions:

Revisions of wording are almost everywhere. Because Zheng's translation often does not conform to colloquial language. To make it clear and fluent on stage, it is necessary to revise the wording at any time. Furthermore, sometimes the wording may conform to colloquial language, but it may not be appropriate for the way the character speaks, and it must be revised. I do not understand Russian, so I can only base my revisions on the translation, striving not to lose the original meaning. The names of people have also been shortened.

The lyrics have all been completely rewritten because the original translation was too long, the sentences were cumbersome, and it was impossible to set them to music. There are also too many songs in the original play, so it was necessary to slightly delete and merge them to avoid being too lengthy on stage. After the deletion and merging, about one-third of the songs were removed, leaving only ten songs, with the most in the second act and only one large chorus in the third act.

The most important revisions are the changes in the plot of the second act. The first act was not changed except for the deletion of two songs. The third act was almost completely unchanged. The second act, in addition to deleting a section, also added a section. The deleted parts were the two old couples among the guests, the old man singing, the person bringing the bear to perform tricks, etc. The added part is Guo Ping's appearance shortly after the opening. Guo Ping did not appear in the original second act.

Ostrovsky wrote this play, paying special attention to expressing the local flavor of Christmas, in addition to the theme. He tried his best to create an atmosphere of Christmas in a village. In the author's intention, he sympathized with the old women and loved those ancient and simple things, contrasting them with the vain Guo Tai and He Lijia. From a national perspective, Guo and his brother, who wasted everything, were very similar, so the author wanted to bring him back.

However, this level of meaning cannot be expressed on the Chinese stage. This kind of local Christmas Eve atmosphere, not to mention that we cannot create it, even if we could, would still be foreign to the Chinese audience. Those songs are folk songs that everyone in Russia knows, so they sound intimate and pleasant, and no one gets tired of them. But it's not the same in China. For example, even if we can find a person and a bear to perform tricks on stage, it will only disrupt the atmosphere of the entire play and will not have any other results. Therefore, we boldly deleted this part.

As I have already said, the original author's efforts to describe the Christmas atmosphere were by no means just to create a lively scene on stage, but to express a contrast between the original simple flavor of the countryside and the superficial civilization that is admired from abroad. The enthusiastic and innocent singing and dancing of the countryside versus the homemade sweet wine and champagne of the Moscow band, the sincere youth of the hometown versus the pseudo-merchants who only pretend to be important—all these are contrasts. Since we have removed the part of the plot that creates the atmosphere, we must find a way to make up for this loss, so as not to reduce the power of the original work. Therefore, we added the scene of Guo Ping's appearance.

This section is based on the last dialogue of the first act. Guo Ping tells Mi Diya that he asked his brother to take him in, but his request was not accepted. So we actually put this into the performance on stage, making the opposition between Guo Tai's and He Lijia's group and the other group, Guo's wife, her daughter, Guo Ping, and even the nanny, more intense, and the conflict between the two sides more obvious. Perhaps the author's original intention can be expressed a little more.

As for the love affair between Mi Diya and Guo Yena, it was originally just a thread to connect the story and was not important. So we still follow the old practice and do not particularly emphasize this part in the direction, but pay more attention to the opposition between the two groups.

We hope that these changes will not cause too much loss to the original play.

Ostrovsky's Immortal Characteristics 232

— Xie Tian

In all aspects, we feel Ostrovsky's unique value. Among the forty works he wrote, each has its own dramatic quality that transcends skill. The characters in each play appear naturally in suitable spaces, and each story develops in a pure and compact manner. The most significant point is that the audience is transparently given each character's consistent personality from beginning to end, and their full and lively expression. We don't need to elaborate, this is his immortal characteristic in the world of playwriting. I believe that he is a theatrical talent made for the stage, and these advantages cannot be compared to those of purely literary figures such as Maeterlinck and Shaw.

From his strengths, I also think of the strengths of China's Water Margin. The 108 heroes of Liangshan in Water Margin each have their own tone. When you see whose words, you know they came from whose mouth. Ostrovsky's script is also like this. Each character appears in the needs of the story and the ideals of the audience, and skillfully uses each person's personality to deal with the environment of the play. There is absolutely no misplaced, unsuitable consciousness casually placed on someone's body. For example, He Lijia and Guo Ping in "Poverty is Not a Crime" are two obvious examples: He Lijia: "I will never let myself be insulted for no reason. You will come and kneel in front of me, asking me to marry your daughter, yes, ha ha ha, you will do this, I know you, you just want a good wedding ceremony, to scare the villagers, you would even be willing to hang yourself, but, no one wants her, how unfortunate ah! Haha!" Guo Ping: "How should I support myself in the big snowstorm?" and "Make way! Guo Ping is gone!"

Ostrovsky has indeed described the characters to a deeply penetrating level.

The entire play of "Poverty is Not a Crime" is also so fittingly portrayed, such as the delicacy of the young people's emotional impulses in the first act, Guo Tai's pursuit of capitalist life in the second and third acts, and the suffering of Mi Diya, Guo's wife, and Guo Yena under the heavy pressure of the feudal system, completely revealing the sins of Russian hypocrisy. (China's current society seems to be like this). Ah, what's more, Ostrovsky is not an artist-for-art's-sake advocate, how should we better determine his value? In China, this decision to perform "Poverty is Not a Crime" by this valuable talent is the first introduction. We feel how appropriate and glorious it is!

Shen Bao Local Supplement

Talk

The Peach Flood is Pressing 233

— Xiaoshan

As the saying goes: "Misfortunes never come singly." China has suffered from the ravages of civil war for years, and is subjected to the oppression of the great powers. The people's livelihood and economy have reached the end of their rope. We can see that the rural and urban economies are bankrupt, and unemployment and hunger are everywhere. Now, floods and droughts are coming even more urgently.

This is a problem worthy of our attention. In the past, the Yellow River flood affected several provinces in the Northwest and North, leaving devastation everywhere. Now, the water level of the Yellow River has risen again. No matter how hard the River Management Committee tries to find ways to rescue the situation, the dam is in a precarious state. What we see is only a palliative method; there is still no fundamental solution. The masses are presented with this "sticking to the old methods" of river management policy, and they have no hope at all. The masses can only wait to die.

In the Yangtze River, we feel the crisis even more. Last year's floods in Hubei and other places caused us immense pain. Let's take a look at the figures: the affected area was 44,870,000 square kilometers, the affected farmland was 70,273,159 mu, the affected population was 7,149,712, the loss of grain was worth 9,063,000 yuan, and the value of cotton was 50,122,200 yuan. This figure is for Hubei Province alone. If we talk about other related provinces, the numbers are truly unimaginable. However, the Yangtze River—especially Hubei Province—is now facing the peach flood again. And it is coming very urgently. We remember that last year, the dike defense work in Hankou, Wuchang, and Hanyang took months of effort, but still could not withstand the flood. This year, the peach flood presents the same crisis. News from Hankou in recent days indicates that the water level is rising, with the water mark recorded above 8.3 meters. From this, it can be seen that last year's flood is likely to occur again.

However, countless people on the brink of death hope that the authorities will not always use the old methods to deal with the situation, but should consider a comprehensive transformation. And for the current transitional dike defense work, it is hoped that special attention will be paid!

The Failure of a Person 234

— Shuman

It's early spring: the sun leisurely spreads over the loose soil in the village that has been ploughed, allowing the crows to jump freely inside, allowing the children to shout and play inside, and allowing the white-haired old people to be lost in thought, reminiscing about the old days: those tears, those laughter, those hardships and difficulties...

The old people have that kind of eccentricity, that kind of habit: in the sunlight, in the afternoon of rainy weather, at dawn and dusk, in midnight dreams, they repeatedly and constantly turn the pages of the book of past life—reminiscing about it, imagining it, chewing on it, like a gluttonous child, greedily swallowing the past life!

"The past has been so long..." A sigh startled the crows resting in the sunlight, causing them to scatter and fly away. Fifth Uncle thought again about those incomprehensible things that seemed dizzying to him—that fate, that life—came: "I am a dying man, fate has hated me all my life, and life is still so difficult..."

"Life is still so difficult," that is indeed true. For example, two years ago, Fifth Uncle was still a rent collector. Although his hair was white and his ears were a little deaf, he relied on his "old age" and the many people he knew, running errands in this small village in the spring and autumn, and life passed by bitterly. "Fate is always against him," as he firmly believed: "Good days will not come. Life is hard, luck is bad, what can be done?"

"Fate!" For this sixty-year-old Fifth Uncle, it has always been a mysterious, great, and incomprehensible thing. He trusted fate all his life, but fate has always been so cruel to him: "Life is hard, there is no way!"

In this "life is hard, there is no way," his dark life crawled slowly like an ox. He believed in fate, he feared hard work, and he retreated from the world from the beginning. When he was young, he did not dare to use his strength to fight for the village girl he loved to be his wife. "Marriage is also destined," so he willingly let his parents arrange a confused marriage for him. At that time, Fifth Uncle had cried twice at night, but later, he quickly forgot everything, because: that was also "fate," people cannot fight against fate—there is no way. (To be continued)

The Completion of National Defense Films 235

— Xinxin

Yesterday, the officials of the Central Propaganda Department summoned the responsible personnel of the Shanghai film industry and held the third discussion meeting in the municipal government. The atmosphere of the meeting was very serious and enthusiastic. The conversation between the host and guests was very close and sincere, making the spirit of sincere cooperation invisibly revealed in the meeting place. For the sake of the future of Chinese films, this is naturally very gratifying.

Reading today's (21st) newspaper, I know that "Regarding the central style of domestic films in the future, the three principles are determined as follows:　Promote national consciousness to fulfill the mission of national defense films;　Carefully select film subjects suitable for the times to promote the effect of film education during national crisis;　The realistic depiction of film plots should fully assist in the advancement of the New Life Movement."

Since the outbreak of the national crisis, progressive and conscientious artists, although in extremely difficult circumstances, have been producing under the goal of "promoting national consciousness to fulfill the mission of national defense films." This is an obvious fact; however, it is regrettable that only a few progressive and conscientious artists are working hard under this goal, while those film producers who are bewitched by the "ice cream theory" are desperately working on the so-called "business vision." Although, in the end, the so-called films full of "business vision" are still not seen to have "business."

Now that the film discussion meeting has such three principles, that is naturally very good. At least, let those "ice cream theorists" also know how much the Central Propaganda Department pays attention to the "effect of film education during national crisis," and how urgently it hopes that the film industry will jointly shoulder the responsibility of "promoting national consciousness to fulfill the mission of national defense films"! At the same time, it also proves how much the responsible personnel of the Shanghai film industry hope that their screenwriters, directors, and other staff will "fulfill the mission of national defense films."

Originally, in today's situation where the national crisis is deepening day by day, the urgent need for "national defense films" has become an indisputable fact, so how should we further complete it?

Speaking of "national defense films," some people will definitely bring up the tail of the Bright Volunteer Army as an excuse for opposition, thinking that "national defense films" are limited to this. So it is summarized into the conclusion that our "national defense films" already exist, but their effect is still not seen, which shows that "national defense films" do not exist. -- Or, use the same reasons for opposing "national defense literature" to oppose "national defense films."

Using the tail of the Bright Volunteer Army to criticize the existence of "national defense films" is obviously a "desperate doctor seeking random treatment" argument. It is certainly ridiculous to formulaically insert a tail of the Volunteer Army, and it is certainly not understanding the diversity of artistic works in terms of content and formal techniques. However, it is not tenable to insist on grasping this weakness as a reason for the non-existence of "national defense films."

And a progressive artist? He will not cling to one subject matter, he understands that under the principle of fighting for national survival, art can correctly reflect this goal. I think this also does not need much explanation from us.

At the discussion meeting, Mr. Ouyang Yuqian raised the issue of "the review of scripts, hoping that the central government has a review scope and writing principles so that screenwriters have something to follow." I think this can also become a problem for the central government to promote the completion of "national defense films." Aren't the three "principles" decided at the discussion meeting just the "principles" to be used as the scope of review and writing?

From this discussion meeting, we not only see the urgent need for "national defense films," but also can see that the central government and the responsible personnel of the film industry both want to "fulfill the mission of national defense films." In addition to hoping that "national defense films" will not become a decoration of this discussion meeting and become "empty talk," we also hope that the central government can handle the script and film review of "national defense films" as quickly and broadly as possible, and also has a way to remedy the double inspection of foreign films!

Except for "ice cream theorists" and those who are bewitched by them, I believe that every conscientious artist will focus on the principle of fighting for national survival to move towards our goal.

He Yunfang He Qinfang Double Pearl Phoenix

China and the West (1040) 1:00 PM to 1:30 PM

Opening "Shepherd's Scroll"

The bandit suppression is successful and returns in glory. Zhu Chundeng is ordered to return to his hometown. Who knows? He doesn't see his wife's face. He hurriedly asks his aunt for her whereabouts. The wolf-hearted woman is eloquent. She says that the mother-in-law and daughter-in-law have gone to the afterlife. Hearing this, he feels as if struck by lightning. He cries his heart out and is filled with hatred. He holds a funeral to help the poor and does good deeds to help the souls of the dead. Who knew? The mother-in-law and daughter-in-law are still alive. They have suffered family disasters and fled to the deep mountains. They live with the shepherds and their flocks. They look at their family but dare not return. They endure tears and beg for food. Husband and wife meet at the tomb. Looking at each other's faces, they are surprised. After a thorough questioning, the truth is revealed. Only then did he know that his aunt had lost her conscience, causing his mother to cry bitterly. On the spot, he changed into official robes and bestowed titles. Hardship is over and sweetness comes, and he can finally smile. The evil woman is anxious at this time. She kneels in the center and makes a vow to dispel suspicion. Who would have thought? Before the vow was finished, a blue dragon arrived. In an instant, her bones turned to ashes. One cannot escape the consequences of one's own evil deeds.

China has a living brain. Taking it can make him healthy. There is no brain juice here. It is inevitable that the scholar will die. Old man, the newly dead can use it. If it can be used, there is still room for discussion. Madam, it can still be used before the seventh day. Taking it can also strengthen him early. Hearing this, Madam Tian split the coffin.

Movies

After the release of "The Trail of the Lonesome Pine" 241

Color film stocks soar instantly. The film is released today at the Grand Theater.

The long-awaited natural color blockbuster, "The Trail of the Lonesome Pine," premiered at the Grand Theater at 9:15 last night. The invention of sound films has already established an immortal miracle in the art of film; and the release of this "The Trail of the Lonesome Pine" will open a new chapter for color films, because this is a natural color film completely shot outdoors, which is different from the dyed films of the past. Other film companies, seeing the success of this experiment, are preparing to shoot important films in color for release. And the colorful film stocks on the New York Stock Exchange soared instantly. The success of this film can be proved by this. Moreover, according to foreign newspaper reviews, this film, even if it is not in color, is a miracle on the screen, because the story is sad and beautiful, and the performances of Sylvia Sidney and others have also achieved great success.
